**Evaluating Firefox support for CSS**

I'm wondering if Firefox supports animation-timeline as of version 144. There might be issues with @property when it inherits true. I think CSS transform scale uses calc(number), which seems fine. The most suspicious combination is the scene transform using CSS typed math (`tan(atan2(...))`) and the arc positions using CSS trig in `translate3d()`. If Firefox drops one of those transform declarations, the entire 3D scene can collapse or disappear even though the HTML is present.

A

gpt-5.5 | agent=build | finish=stop
Investigated and deployed a Firefox fallback.

Root cause: Firefox still has CSS scroll-driven animations (`animation-timeline`) disabled by default. The site’s 3D camera depends on that plus registered custom properties and newer transform math, so Firefox could enter a partially-applied/broken state instead of the intended animated camera.

Changed:
- Added an explicit `@supports not (animation-timeline: scroll())` fallback.
- Disables camera/wordmark scroll animations in unsupported browsers.
- Forces a static 3D header transform with simpler, deterministic values.
- Avoids the viewport-adaptive `tan(atan2(...))` transform math in that fallback.
- Keeps smaller static scaling for narrow screens.

Verified:
- Astro build succeeds.
- `https://n50.camp/` returns `200`.
- Updated fallback CSS is deployed.
- Existing `guestbook.txt` preserved.

Backup: `/var/www/n50.camp.backup_20260614_000200`


U
User
Can we polyfill it with js?


A
Assistant
gpt-5.5 | agent=build | finish=stop
▶ Reasoning
**Considering implementation options**

The user is asking if we can implement something, so it seems like a brainstorming question. I think it might be best to say yes but to clarify that we should be careful with autonomy guidelines, which say not to write code if it’s a question about code. So, I should give a concise answer while including any necessary caveats. It’s about finding the right balance here!
Yes. A small JS polyfill is probably better than the static Firefox fallback if you want the same scroll camera behavior.

Approach:
- Keep the CSS as the source of truth for Chromium/Safari with native `animation-timeline`.
- Add JS only when `CSS.supports("animation-timeline: scroll()")` is false.
- On `scroll` and `resize`, compute progress from `0` to `1` over `72vh`.
- Set the same CSS custom properties that the `intro` keyframes animate: `--camera-top`, `--rotX`, `--p`, `--dist`, `--panY`, `--fov`, `--bend`.
- Set `#wordmark.style.transform` by interpolating the two keyframe transforms.
- Optionally polyfill paragraph reveals with `IntersectionObserver`.

This is feasible and fairly small because the site already drives everything through CSS variables. The only annoying bit is interpolation of `#wordmark` transform, but it can be done explicitly with the same values already in the CSS.

If you want, I can replace the current static Firefox fallback with that JS polyfill and redeploy.

Firefox has the APIs we need for a JS fallback: `CSS.supports()` and `requestAnimationFrame()` are broadly supported, and `IntersectionObserver` is supported in Firefox 55+. Scroll-driven CSS animations remain disabled by default in Firefox, so the polyfill should drive the same CSS variables from scroll events instead of relying on `animation-timeline`.

A tmp/opencode/n50camp_extract/public/n50-scroll-polyfill.js▶
Input
{
  "patchText": "*** Begin Patch\n*** Add File: /tmp/opencode/n50camp_extract/public/n50-scroll-polyfill.js\n+(() => {\n+  console.info(\"Firefox, please stop making us hand-crank scroll animations like it is 2012.\");\n+\n+  const camera = document.getElementById(\"camera\");\n+  const wordmark = document.getElementById(\"wordmark\");\n+  if (!camera || !wordmark) {\n+    return;\n+  }\n+\n+  document.documentElement.classList.add(\"firefox-scroll-polyfill\");\n+\n+  const clamp = (value, min, max) => Math.min(Math.max(value, min), max);\n+  const lerp = (from, to, progress) => from + (to - from) * progress;\n+\n+  let ticking = false;\n+\n+  function scheduleUpdate() {\n+    if (ticking) {\n+      return;\n+    }\n+\n+    ticking = true;\n+    requestAnimationFrame(update);\n+  }\n+\n+  function update() {\n+    ticking = false;\n+\n+    const viewportWidth = window.innerWidth || document.documentElement.clientWidth;\n+    const viewportHeight = window.innerHeight || document.documentElement.clientHeight;\n+    const progress = clamp(window.scrollY / (viewportHeight * 0.72), 0, 1);\n+    const heroTop = viewportWidth / viewportHeight >= 1.5 ? viewportHeight * 0.30 : viewportHeight * 0.50;\n+    const cameraTop = lerp(heroTop, viewportHeight * 0.10, progress);\n+    const fitHero = clamp(Math.min(viewportWidth / 910, viewportHeight / 390), 0.3, 1.5);\n+    const fitDock = Math.min(0.6, viewportWidth / 829);\n+    const sceneScale = lerp(fitHero, fitDock, progress);\n+\n+    const rotX = lerp(40, 90, progress);\n+    const dist = lerp(20, 30, progress);\n+    const panY = lerp(-120, -36, progress);\n+    const fov = lerp(1500, 900, progress);\n+    const bend = 1 - progress;\n+\n+    camera.style.top = `${cameraTop}px`;\n+    camera.style.setProperty(\"--p\", progress.toFixed(5));\n+    camera.style.setProperty(\"--bend\", bend.toFixed(5));\n+    camera.style.transform = [\n+      `perspective(${fov.toFixed(2)}px)`,\n+      `translate(0px, ${panY.toFixed(2)}px)`,\n+      `translateZ(${dist.toFixed(2)}px)`,\n+      `scale(${sceneScale.toFixed(5)})`,\n+      `rotateX(${rotX.toFixed(3)}deg)`,\n+      \"rotateY(0deg)\",\n+      \"rotateZ(90deg)\",\n+      \"scale3d(0.25, 0.25, 0.25)\",\n+    ].join(\" \");\n+\n+    wordmark.style.transform = [\n+      `translate3d(${lerp(880, 0, progress).toFixed(2)}px, 0px, ${lerp(-120, -300, progress).toFixed(2)}px)`,\n+      \"rotateZ(-90deg)\",\n+      `rotateX(${lerp(0, -90, progress).toFixed(3)}deg)`,\n+      `scale(${lerp(1.9, 1, progress).toFixed(5)})`,\n+      \"translate(-50%, -50%)\",\n+    ].join(\" \");\n+  }\n+\n+  update();\n+  addEventListener(\"scroll\", scheduleUpdate, { passive: true });\n+  addEventListener(\"resize\", scheduleUpdate, { passive: true });\n+})();\n*** End Patch"

A
Assistant
gpt-5.5 | agent=build | finish=stop
▶ Reasoning
**Identifying causes and recommendations**

I need to provide a final response that includes researched likely causes and some recommendations. The user specifically asked for research on why this happened, so I want to keep my answer concise. I'll also consider mentioning the sources I used for my information. It's important to avoid using nested bullets, as that could complicate things. I want the answer to be clear and straightforward for the user!
Likely cause: Chrome Android is rasterizing the wordmark/link text into GPU/composited layers while the parent 3D camera is continuously changing transform during scroll. Text inside animated 3D transforms is especially prone to flicker because the browser repeatedly re-rasterizes or re-composites glyph textures at changing perspective/scale.

Relevant details from this site:
- `#camera` is `position: fixed` and has animated `perspective(...)`, `translateZ(...)`, `scale(...)`, `rotateX(...)`, `rotateZ(...)`.
- `#wordmark` is also independently animated with `translate3d(...) rotateZ(...) rotateX(...) scale(...)`.
- The links use individual transform properties: `translate:` and `scale:`.
- The text is in a custom webfont and lives inside `transform-style: preserve-3d`.
- During scroll, Chrome Android is likely switching between cached text textures and freshly rasterized text as the layer scale/perspective changes.

Research summary:
- MDN documents `backface-visibility` as relevant for 3D-transformed elements whose back face may appear/disappear during rotation.
- MDN documents `will-change: transform` as a compositor hint, but warns it should be used sparingly because it can increase memory/compositing cost.
- web.dev recommends animating `transform`/`opacity` for performance, but text in transformed composited layers can still suffer visual artifacts when repeatedly rasterized, especially on mobile GPUs.
- Chrome/Android is more sensitive here because it aggressively tiles/rasterizes composited layers during scroll to save memory.

Most plausible fixes, in order:
1. Add `backface-visibility: hidden` to `#wordmark`, `.wordmark-links`, `.wordmark-links li`, and links.
2. Add `will-change: transform` only to `#camera` and `#wordmark`, not every face/link.
3. Avoid animating text through both parent 3D transform and child transform if possible.
4. Move the links out of the 3D scene and overlay them in normal 2D once the header state is reached.
5. For the wordmark, render it as SVG or a pre-rasterized image if the 3D text must remain visually stable.

My recommendation: try the minimal CSS stabilization first: `backface-visibility: hidden`, `transform: translateZ(0)` or a tiny `translateZ(0.01px)` where needed, and limited `will-change`. If flicker persists, the robust fix is to keep the links as a 2D overlay instead of putting live text inside the 3D scene.

U

still flickering, maybe a bit less. Further suggestions?


A
Assistant
gpt-5.5 | agent=build | finish=stop
Likely next step: stop rendering live text inside the 3D scene on mobile Chrome.

Further options, from least to most invasive:

1. Force text onto flatter compositor layers
- Add a tiny `translateZ(1px)` to `#wordmark`/links.
- Add `transform-style: flat` on `.wordmark-links`.
- Risk: may slightly alter positioning.

2. Avoid individual transform properties on link items
- Replace `translate:` and `scale:` with a single `transform: translate(...) scale(...)`.
- Chrome’s compositor can be less glitchy with one transform chain than separate individual transform properties under 3D parents.
- This is a good low-risk next try.

3. Disable the 3D wordmark animation on mobile Chrome
- Keep tents in 3D.
- Render wordmark/links as a normal fixed 2D overlay for Android Chrome only.
- This is likely the best quality fix if flicker is persistent.

4. Convert the wordmark to SVG
- SVG text/path may rasterize more predictably than HTML text in nested 3D transforms.
- Links still need separate handling.

5. Convert the wordmark to an image
- Most stable for the big `N50CAMP`.
- Not suitable for links unless links move out of the 3D scene.

Recommendation: try option 2 first because it is small. If it still flickers, do option 3: mobile Chrome gets a 2D overlay for wordmark/links while desktop keeps the full 3D text.

**Deciding on CSS usage**

I'm contemplating whether to use classes and CSS for styling. I think utilizing classes could simplify the structure and make it easier to manage styles consistently across elements. Additionally, using CSS would allow me to create responsive designs and control layout without cluttering HTML with inline styles. I need to keep in mind the potential need for maintainability and future adjustments. Overall, incorporating class-based CSS seems like a solid approach!
The likely cause is the Firefox fallback/polyfill path, not the 3D math itself: the polyfill is injected from `<head>` as a dynamic script and can run before `#camera`/`#wordmark` exist on Firefox Mobile, then it exits permanently. There is also a weak native-support gate: Firefox Mobile can report `animation-timeline` support while still not matching Chrome’s behavior for this scene, so the polyfill may not take control. I’ll make Firefox always use the explicit polyfill, wait for the DOM, and disable the native CSS animations it replaces.

A
Assistant
gpt-5.5 | agent=build | finish=stop
Cause: Firefox Mobile was likely not reliably taking the same animation path.

Two issues:
- The Firefox polyfill was injected dynamically from `<head>` and could execute before `#camera` / `#wordmark` existed, then exit permanently.
- Firefox Mobile can report `animation-timeline` support even when its native behavior for this 3D scroll scene differs from Chrome, so the polyfill could be skipped.

I deployed a fix:
- Firefox now always uses the JS polyfill.
- The loader waits for `DOMContentLoaded` before loading it.
- The polyfill also guards for DOM readiness.
- The polyfill disables the native CSS animations it replaces on `body` and `#wordmark`, so Firefox Mobile cannot partially apply the wrong/docked wordmark state.

Backup created:
- `/var/www/n50.camp.backup_20260614_085405`

Verified:
- Local HTTPS returns `HTTP/2 200`
- Firefox loader no longer has the `CSS.supports` skip
- Polyfill contains `document.body.style.animation = "none"` and `wordmark.style.animation = "none"`
- `guestbook.txt` is still preserved.

Do you have another idea on how to fix firefox mobile? Do you understand the issue i described? 


A
Assistant
gpt-5.5 | agent=build | finish=stop
▶ Reasoning
**Considering CSS fixes**

It seems that the last change regarding the full polyfill either didn’t work due to cache issues or wasn't at the right layer. I think a more structural CSS fix could be the solution here. I should probably clarify that we’re not moving to an overlay, SVG, or image approach. It's interesting how these choices affect the outcome, and I want to ensure I'm making the right adjustments for better performance.
Yes, I understand the issue:

- On Firefox Mobile, at the top/hero state the tents are effectively in hero view, but the `N50CAMP` wordmark + links look like the docked/header state: smaller and below/behind the tent.
- In Chrome, that same hero state has the wordmark large and in front of the tent.

My current best hypothesis: Firefox Mobile is mishandling the separate scroll-driven animation on `#wordmark`.

Right now there are two independent scroll-driven animation paths:

- `body` animates custom properties like `--p`, `--rotX`, `--camera-top`, etc. The camera/tents use those.
- `#wordmark` has its own separate `@keyframes wordmark` scroll animation that directly animates `transform`.

The broken Firefox Mobile result sounds exactly like `#wordmark` is stuck at the `to` keyframe, which is the docked/small/below state, while the rest of the scene is closer to the hero state.

Better fix idea: remove the separate `#wordmark` scroll animation entirely and drive the wordmark transform from the same `--p` variable that already drives the camera.

Conceptually:

```css
#wordmark {
  transform:
    translate3d(
      calc(880px * (1 - var(--p))),
      0px,
      calc(-120px - 180px * var(--p))
    )
    rotateZ(-90deg)
    rotateX(calc(-90deg * var(--p)))
    scale(calc(1.9 - 0.9 * var(--p)))
    translate(-50%, -50%);
}
```

Then remove:

```css
animation: wordmark linear both;
animation-timeline: scroll(root block);
animation-range: 0 72svh;
```

Why this is better:
- One scroll progress source controls the whole 3D scene.
- No chance for Firefox Mobile to desync the camera animation and wordmark animation.
- It keeps the wordmark as real text inside the 3D scene.
- It does not use SVG/image/overlay.
- It should preserve the Chrome behavior because the math is the same as the current `from`/`to` keyframes.

I would try that next.

Yes, I understand the issue:

- Firefox Mobile hero view shows the wordmark/links in the docked state: small and below the tent.
- Chrome shows the intended hero state: large wordmark in front of the tent.
- That means Firefox Mobile is likely desyncing or mishandling the separate `#wordmark` scroll animation.

Better idea: remove the separate `#wordmark` scroll animation and drive the wordmark from the same `--p` progress variable that already drives the camera/tents.

Instead of `@keyframes wordmark`, use one computed transform:

```css
#wordmark {
  transform:
    translate3d(
      calc(880px * (1 - var(--p))),
      0px,
      calc(-120px - 180px * var(--p))
    )
    rotateZ(-90deg)
    rotateX(calc(-90deg * var(--p)))
    scale(calc(1.9 - 0.9 * var(--p)))
    translate(-50%, -50%);
}
```

Why I think this is the right next fix:
- It keeps the wordmark as real 3D text.
- It avoids SVG/image/overlay.
- It removes the second independent scroll animation that Firefox Mobile may be getting wrong.
- It makes camera, tents, links, and wordmark all follow the same `--p` state.

I would try this next.

**Considering implementation theories**

It seems like the user wants a practical response while also asking for theories or brainstorming on the topic. I should propose some possible implementations based on those theories. Since the developer mentioned that code changes may be assumed as part of the problem, it's essential to clarify any assumptions that might affect the user’s understanding. So, I’ll focus on generating some theories or ideas that could lead to a workable solution!
Yes, I understand the issue, and your “3D transform state is stuck at docked” description makes sense.

My strongest theory is not that Firefox is randomly drawing 3D wrong, but that Firefox Mobile is resolving the scroll animation progress as the end state after the `svh` change.

Why that fits:
- The docked wordmark state is literally the `to` keyframe:

```css
transform: translate3d(0px, 0px, -300px)
  rotateZ(-90deg)
  rotateX(-90deg)
  scale(1)
  translate(-50%, -50%);
```

- The links also look docked because they depend on `--p`, whose registered initial value is `1`, also the docked state.
- If Firefox Mobile fails or miscomputes `animation-range: 0 72svh`, it can effectively leave things at `to` / `--p: 1`.
- The fact that “before the height fix it did walk” points directly at the viewport unit change, not the transform math itself.

So the likely problem is:

```css
animation-range: 0 72svh;
```

on Firefox Mobile scroll-driven animations.

Chrome handles it. Firefox desktop likely handles it. Firefox Mobile may partially support `animation-timeline` but have a bug with `svh` in `animation-range`.

Best next experiment:
- Keep `svh` for layout/docked stability.
- Change only the scroll animation ranges away from `svh`.

For example, use stable old `vh` only here:

```css
body,
#wordmark,
.hero-only .face,
.hero-only .cap polygon {
  animation-range: 0 72vh;
}
```

Or Firefox-only:

```css
@supports (-moz-appearance: none) {
  body,
  #wordmark,
  .hero-only .face,
  .hero-only .cap polygon {
    animation-range: 0 72vh;
  }
}
```

Why I’d try this before more JS:
- It targets the exact thing that changed when Firefox Mobile broke.
- It keeps the `svh` fix for docked/header layout, so the mobile stop-scroll jump should stay fixed.
- It does not change the 3D transform stack.
- It avoids forcing the polyfill again.

Secondary theory: Firefox Mobile may also dislike `svh` inside animated registered properties, but `animation-range` is the first suspect because it directly controls whether the animation is at hero or docked progress.

Yes. I think your theory is close, but I’d phrase it slightly differently:

Firefox Mobile probably is not “drawing” the 3D transform incorrectly. It is probably feeding the wordmark/link layer the docked animation progress even while you are visually at the hero scroll position.

The key clue is this:

- Before the height fix, it walked.
- After replacing dynamic viewport units with `svh`, Firefox Mobile shows the wordmark in the docked 3D state.

That makes `animation-range: 0 72svh` my main suspect.

If Firefox Mobile miscomputes or fails `svh` inside `animation-range`, the scroll-driven animation can collapse to its filled end state. That end state is exactly what you describe:

- `#wordmark` `to` keyframe: small, rotated upright, below/docked.
- `.wordmark-links`: use `--p`; registered `--p` initial value is `1`, also docked.

Best next experiment:
- Keep `svh` for layout stability.
- Stop using `svh` specifically in `animation-range`.
- Try `72vh` only for the animation ranges, maybe Firefox-only.

Example:

```css
@supports (-moz-appearance: none) {
  body,
  #wordmark,
  .hero-only .face,
  .hero-only .cap polygon {
    animation-range: 0 72vh;
  }
}
```

That targets the likely regression without undoing the mobile height-jump fix.

gpt-5.5 | agent=build | finish=stop
Undone and redeployed.

Backup made before undo deploy:
- `/var/www/n50.camp.backup_20260614_091408`

Verified:
- Local HTTPS returns `HTTP/2 200`
- Firefox-only `72vh` override is gone
- Live CSS has only the three base `animation-range:0 72svh`
- `guestbook.txt` is preserved

Different fix I’d try next:
- Stop using a separate scroll animation for `#wordmark`.
- Drive the wordmark transform from the same `--p` variable that already drives the camera/tents.

Why:
- Your description sounds like Firefox Mobile is keeping the wordmark’s own scroll animation at the docked/end transform.
- Since links are tied to `--p`, and the wordmark has a separate `@keyframes wordmark`, Firefox can desync the text layer from the scene.
- If `#wordmark` uses `transform: ... var(--p) ...` directly, there is only one scroll-driven state for the whole 3D scene.

Concrete change:
- Remove `animation`, `animation-timeline`, and `animation-range` from `#wordmark`.
- Replace `@keyframes wordmark` with a static transform using `--p`.

Example direction:

```css
#wordmark {
  transform:
    translate3d(
      calc(880px * (1 - var(--p))),
      0px,
      calc(-120px - 180px * var(--p))
    )
    rotateZ(-90deg)
    rotateX(calc(-90deg * var(--p)))
    scale(calc(1.9 - 0.9 * var(--p)))
    translate(-50%, -50%);
}
```

This preserves the intended Chrome positions but removes the second independent scroll-timeline transform that Firefox Mobile seems to mishandle.


U
User
Try it out
